< text>
Our family loves Gyminny Kids.  We joined about 1 year ago.  We were referred by Ronna.

Staff:  All staff members, especially Ronna, are super sweet and friendly.  They always greet my kids.  My daughter had Ms. Larissa and now has Mr. Earl.  She likes both teachers and I do too.  They are great with the kids.  My 4 year old daughter loves Gyminny Kids so much that she requested to have her 4th birthday party here last month in September.  Ronna kindly helped us with setting the arrangement up. The staff at the birthday party was great! We picked the princess theme.  Staff members that assisted us dressed up as princess/prince characters.  They decorated the room with table cloth, disney princess plates, disney princess center pieces, disney princess cups, and disney princess tiara.  They allowed me to bring my own decorations and cake as well.  I did bring some food too for the guest.  The party was 1 1/2 hours which I felt was perfect.  Parents enjoyed the birthday party because they had 1 hour to sit and enjoy other adults while watching their kids have fun with the staff.  Everything was executed well from greeting all guest at the birthday, getting the gifts, giving them name tags, putting them in groups, doing the activity for 1 hour, then leading the kids to the party room, and then leading them down to the front entrance once it was done.

Parking: there are plenty of spots in the parking lot.

Fee: it's pretty reasonable for the amount of fun my daughter has.

Environment/activities: they do so many activities that really allow the child to be engaged.  It assist with development and gross motor skills as well. The facility is big with a lot of equipment.  Staff members assist throughout the whole time in their class.  They have different themes every week where staff members dress up.  The facility is pretty clean and opened.  There are a lot of seats for the parent to watch the kids from the second floor deck.

I highly recommend this place.<//text>

< Review>
LOVE THIS PLACE!
I'm an Italian au pair currently living in the States and tonight I came here to have dinner with my host family. First time having dinner out since I got here.
I couldn't have had better night.
I had Gnocchi al Gorgonzola and gosh, those were delicious, almost tasted like home if it wasn't for the parmesan cause there was too much but I LOVED them!
Then I fell in love with the Buttercream Cake with Vanilla Ice Cream on top.
The kids didn't eat everything so we bought the leftovers home!

The staff was so nice and kind and we had so much fun talking with them!
Alexandria served us and she was amazing! This is the kind of staff I like to meet when I go to a restaurant.

THANK YOU SO MUCH FOR HAVING US!
I'll definitely be back to have that buttercream cake again!üòç< /Review>

Deering Dorla</user_name>
< review>
A cute looking little house with seating on the porch and L-shaped patio, and more modern little restaurant (and kitchen) behind it.  So cute, it was my gf's and my choice for our first time in downtown Danville.  That means, it stood out above all others, and it was good to take our pooch since we could sit nicely outside on the patio.

However, we were put off by the lifeless hostess who clearly didn't like people and didn't want to be there.  Then, we sat at our table without acknowledgement for at least 5-7 minutes, until another gal with water didn't say hello and just went with the task at hand.  Finally, our server, was good but was 18 at best, and no fault of his, not mature.

The food was remarkably good.  We had the Lasagne di Carne [$21, 4.0 stars] -- a good portion, and very good Bolognese Sauce; Carni Suprema [$17, 4.5 stars] -- wonderful crust, but a little sparse with the toppings (Meatballs, Calabrese Sausage, Pepperoni) and a little small.  Still, very good and worthy.

So, in the end, won't likely return.  Food 8/10 and service 3/10.<//review>

<date>1503279316372<//date><Rating>5</Rating>< text>
I love Comicopolis! I live a couple of hundred miles away so I don't get to visit as often as I'd like but you can bet I keep my comic book fund handy whenever I know I'm making a trip up the coast.
The store itself is super clean and organized, with the shelves jam packed with amazing books (and games!).
One of the owners, Troy (we haven't met the other one), is super friendly and welcoming as well as suuuper knowledgeable regarding all things comics. He always takes the time to help each and every customer find exactly what they're looking for and he always has awesome suggestions.

My partner and I have been loyal customers of comicopolis for 5 ish years now and have no intent to stop because we love giving our business to a shop that's owned by true comic book nerds who love what they do.

Keep up the good work guys!!< /text>

<date>1531459598603< /date><Rate>1<//Rate>< Review>
You know how when you order Chinese food you don't worry about getting too much because you`ll want left overs?  I picked up some take out while in town to take home 45 miles away.   The house fried rice and the cashew chicken with all of their many different ingredients was so unfresh both dishes were just grey.   The only thing with color was scrambled eggs which led me to believe everything else was frozen at some point, probably to long based on the funny taste.
The fried prawns , which I always get at any Chinese restaurant with spicy mustard,  would have definitely been sent back if I were served them in house.  No where near fresh AND hard.
The Hunan beef was watery and tasteless.  Hmmm,  sounds like reheated frozen food to me.
Didn`t even try the house chow mien;  Same grey color.
Smelled great all the way home!   Didn`t finish what I put on my plate and threw the rest in the garbage.     $75 with 15% tip.  Saddened me because I noticed one of the original family girls still there.
I`ve never written a review where everything was terrible but it was.
I`d rather be writing a great review and dreaming about awesome leftovers.  No excuse for this disregard of quality control.
Sadly, never again.</Review>

< review>
Came here for lunch one day. Store has enough seating. Portion size is decent. The menu is okay. I think there shouldn't be an extra charge for the salad because most places don't charge extra for it. The avocado charge is fine, there seems to be a "shortage" of it in CA, must be too many ppl ordering avocado toast =P

The fish ingredients were soggy. The octopus is rubbery, which means it wasn't cooked properly. When I tried the brown rice, it was really dry. The place is close to a lot of apartments so I bet they get lots of customers that way but overall, it's okay. Definitely not the worst, just average.

The bowls  need to be larger to better accommodate the ability to mix the ingredients ourselves. Otherwise, a lot will just fall out. I am still on the hunt for an excellent poke place in SD.</review>

107431159307221735908< /userid>
<Name>Kelly Parks</Name><Time>1559754346842< /Time><rating>5</rating>< Review>
Kazanori is a super solid poke spot in Westfield UTC!! It's kinda tucked away in the corner next to Rubio'a so it can be a little easy to miss.

They offer a good amount of option for protein and many of them are already marinated! I tried two scoops of the crunchy garlic tuna and the salmon and liked both a lot! I also got masago, seaweed salad, carrots and edamame. The veggies are pretty low frills and you can expect all the usual toppings. The spicy aioli was really yummy and comparable to spicy mayo! Really brought the whole bowl together for me.

UTC is annoying now and only has 2 free hours of parking so shopping and eating is a little tough if you're trying to stay in that window. Kazanori makes it a little easier though by providing quick and friendly service!<//Review>

<rate>4<//rate><text>It's my first time getting a poke bowl. This Hawaiian dish is pretty much a tasty sashimi bowl. Poke UTC is another fast casual restaurant. You start off picking your base: white rice, brown rice, chips, or salad. Then you get 2 scoops of raw fish (salmon, tuna, spicy tuna, yellowtail, scallops) and pick what you want mixed in (imitation crab, cucumber, white onion; avocado and seaweed salad are extra cost). Finish it off with your sauce (poke sauce, spicy mayo, ponzu) and toppings (cilantro, green onions, sesame seeds, etc).

For my bowl, I chose salmon, tuna, avocado, white onions, cilantro, and green onions. I went with the spicy mayo because that's what the employee recommended. The scallops didn't look very fresh. The quality of the fish was alright, but my bowl as a whole was enjoyable. I'm a huge fan of salmon so this is my kind of dish. It was a filling meal for a $10 meal. I wish we had some poke shops here in DC, MD, VA.

Service was friendly and helpful. If you're a first timer, they'll explain the process to you.< /text>< pictures>

1477092685885<//time>
< rate>
3<//rate>
<review>You ever had a bagel in NYC? Then you know what we have on the west coast is training wheels compared to them. Well the same can be said about most San Diego poke, it's good-ish, but is B Squad compared to the real stuff.

Poke, oh poke, how when in Hawaii you are so delicious and tasty, but her in California you are a new genre of food I call Chipoke. The build your own bowl style like they do at chipotle. It's not that this is "authentic", but the hot calrose rise. Of all the poke at family parties, never once was it served over rice. It's really more of a side dish, but yeah if you want to make it into a meal, by all means put some rice on it, just use the right rice. I'm pretty sure the Japanese restaurants get this right by using sushi rice. Brown rice, of course California, of course. Salad, of course California. My poke salad's at most Japanese restaurants are frugal with the salad, it's not even a base or the main ingredient, so easy guys.

D√©cor, blah, strip mall in La Jolla's University City. About has Hawaii as the Mai Tai you get at TGIF, not UTC like the name states, so don't go to the mall and think it's in the food court. Should be called Poke University City. Service is quite good, friendly fast, very consistent in portions. Not much in the way of competition, so their pricing is questionable. Even with extra free accoutrements the small is not very filling. The sauces are pretty mild, top to bottom. I like the liberal use of sesame seeds, but not the overuse of green onions. I dig the mac salad, something missing from most places and the daikon, excellent offerings. The fish is fresh, firm. The dishes turn out good looking, but to me taste should not be sacrificed for appearance. My tastebuds and stomach don't see pretty like in all the pics with the vibrant colors and good lighting.

Some ingredients are extra like Avo and seaweed salad. If I'm eating rice with my fish I'm trying to be healthy, and part of that is the ratio, don't overload the bowl with rice and pile the fish on top making it look like it's overflowing. I'd rather have a sensible ratio of fish to rice and even accoutrements to rice and fish. The sauces have to be better, more bold, they have to use more and it has to coat things better.

I work in a deadzone for poke and burgers and Mexican food and half of what I used to eat weekly, so I'm severely disappointed when I get mediocre food driving all the way from Carmel Valley. Most of San Diego, heck Southern California poke has let me down in someway, this more than others. i gave an extra star because of consistency, but this makes me miss Hawaii.</review>< Pictures>
None< /Pictures>

< Review>
Nice small restaurant in a nice small town. Easy to locate & find parking. I ordered the falafel wrap & a side of fries for 2 people. There was plenty of food for a meal & there were fries leftover for later. Everything was served hot and fresh and tasted delicious. The falafel wrap had the perfect assortment of flavors and the right amount of each ingredient. Good customer service, too. Would definitely visit again.<//Review>

< Text>
1 Star meal: not even the manager, after issuing me a full refund, could tell me what this menu item was (no.9). Served warn, not hot. And bland, oh my was it bland.

1 Star service: I believe our server was given too many tables to serve. The result being I felt rushed, not heard, and in the end forgotten.

1 Star management: I had to come back twice to receive a refund. The first time I asked for a refund, the person in charge said I needed come back to speak with someone else.

When I came back the next day to see that person, to my dismay, the servers pointed out that same person I spoke with the other day. They said the guy I'm looking for is the one wearing the red shirt, sitting in the circle of men smoking cigars. Yep, it was the same guy from the day before. The same guy who told me I needed to speak to someone else. Well, he walked me back to the restaurant and gave me a refund.

I believe, depending on what day you go, what time of day or night you go, who is cooking that day or night, and how busy they are will determine the quality of the meal and level of service you will receive. Hence the wide range of reviewing experiences, all of which I believe true.<//Text>

< text>
Another Cuban restaurant that has lost what they once were.  Ever since the Father passed the manner in which they cut corners on cooking the food saddens me.  Saturday was and is Garbanzo Bean soup day. Best soup I've eaten besides my moms.  Buuttt... Now they are using canned garbanzo beans instead of the original way they use to do it. How can one tell.... The beans are stiff and hard and they do not let it simmer long enough to obtain the flavor of the seasoning  or the bean to open properly.  Too bad it is a rare gem being lost.  Ramon we or I miss your dedication to making your customers happy with the quality of food and service<//text>

< review>
Absolutely one of the best bargains between San Diego and Los Angeles. The food is excellent and the service is better than 99% of restaurants within their price range out there.  Don't ask what to order, follow your heart - it's just THAT good.  My go to is the red snapper- but it's no ordinary dish.  The entire staff is like family.  They are loyal to the owners and loyal to the customers, many who've been going there for over 25 years.  This is not just a restaurant, it's an iconic American venue</review>

<text>Great food, good cultural experience, good location. Doesn't have own parking, public parking available but not close to restaurant. Place is a little tight, ambience lacking, but you go there for the food and experience.< /text><username>Amado Carino< /username>< Rating>

</record></dataset><record>
<user>112209497970523732050< /user>< username>
Jeffrey Dickman<//username>
<date>1527727365901< /date><rating>4</rating>< review>
I've eaten at Felix's for thirty years. It remains a very consistent restaurant, and one where the locals eat. A nice selection of meat, fish and chicken Cuban cuisine. Most meals begin about $13. For that one gets a hearty bowl of soup, or small salad, bread, the entree and one of three desserts. I like the plain Chicken Cubano, a half a roasted bird, a big helping of delicious rice, black beans and plantains. If you like a warm green sauce ask for it on the side. My wife enjoys the rice and chicken with vegetables. I do not eat meat, however traditional pork and beef dishes are plentiful on the menu. I like to pay for a slice of their homemade chocolate cake and then take home the dessert which comes with the meal for a snack the next day. Enjoy your meal with a drink of wine or a beer.

Try the breakfasts, many of which come with either a Tostada Latina, two slices of batter cooked french bread with a guava puree between, or the Fritter, a sort of cooked pastry ball with a sweet sauce. Most breakfasts are between $10 and $14. You can eat well for $10. Most breakfasts also include a small juice.

Service is good, people are nice and helpful. It's located in the Orange Circle. Parking is more easily found beyond the circle in several adjoining parking lots.

Try Felix's once and you'll likely return.< /review>

< name>
dave mauzey<//name>
<Date>1358214388248< /Date>< rate>
2<//rate>
< Text>
If you like cuban cuisine this might be a good place. It was crowded (which is a good sign)

Did not go inside, but that was mostly due to the cold temperatures outside and everyone was in there trying to get away from the cold air.
So we had to settle with outside and the heat lamps of which there were too few and not in good placement.

But if you like Spanish cuisine, im not so sure this is the one for you. My preference is PAELLA, I really know what works and what doesn't. The Paella (Valencia) in particular did not even come near my standards or even what is the standard to expect.

I know there are a lot of variations but this just was let me simply say this... NO!

The rice was more of a soggy mess, and was way too much. It overwhelmed the seafood and there was no socrate or socarrat. Speaking of seafood, (only one mussel), no clams (that I could make out), the shrimp was good (4), a few squid (no tentacles) and the fish was so mashed I could not find any decent pieces, the sausage (was more of a chorizo) had no business in there)

So if you like Paella don't eat that here, anything else perhaps but I will seek my dining in the downtown city of orange elsewhere and my Paella at other places I have been.< /Text>
